- **feat(scripts,tasks,skills): pre-merge Greptile-body verdict gate (`task pr:merge-ready`)** (refs #796, refs #526) -- closes the SUCCESS-with-findings blind spot in the swarm Phase 5 -> 6 merge-readiness checklist. New `scripts/pr_merge_readiness.py` parses the Greptile rolling-summary comment **body** (not the GitHub `Greptile Review` CheckRun status) and exits non-zero when the PR is not merge-ready. The CheckRun goes green when Greptile finishes its review pass irrespective of confidence score or P0 / P1 findings; relying on it alone is what started the PR #652 merge-cascade incident against `Confidence: 3/5 + 1×P1 + 2×P2`. The script asserts: HEAD-SHA freshness (`Last reviewed commit:` markdown-link form mirrors the canonical regex from `templates/swarm-greptile-poller-prompt.md`), errored-sentinel absence (#526 `Greptile encountered an error while reviewing this PR`), `Confidence Score: X/5` parsed AND > 3, and zero P0 / P1 findings via HTML severity-badge counting (`<img alt="P0"`, `<img alt="P1"`) with a structured-section heading fallback (`### P0 findings (N)`). P2 findings are non-blocking per `skills/deft-directive-review-cycle/SKILL.md` Phase 2 Step 6 and do NOT gate the loop. The badge-count approach is robust by construction against the negation-context false positive (clean-summary phrasing `No P0 or P1 issues found` contains the literal P0 / P1 tokens, which a raw substring scan would flag -- the badges appear ONLY on actual findings). Three-state exit (0 merge-ready / 1 merge-blocked / 2 external error) matches the convention of `scripts/pr_check_protected_issues.py` (#702) and `scripts/pr_check_closing_keywords.py` (#737). New `tasks/pr.yml::merge-ready` Taskfile target wraps `uv run python scripts/pr_merge_readiness.py {{.CLI_ARGS}}` (no `sources:` / `generates:` per `conventions/task-caching.md` -- `--repo` and `--json` are user-facing flags). `skills/deft-directive-swarm/SKILL.md` Phase 5 -> 6 merge-readiness checklist gains a `!` MUST rule requiring `task pr:merge-ready -- <N>` to be invoked before each `gh pr merge` call (abort the cascade on non-zero exit) plus a `⊗` MUST NOT rule against merging on the basis of a SUCCESS Greptile CheckRun alone (the symmetric blind spot to the existing #526 NEUTRAL-CheckRun anti-pattern). Anti-Patterns block gains a corresponding bullet citing the PR #652 incident. New `tests/cli/test_pr_merge_readiness.py` (23 tests) covers parser correctness (clean body / badge findings / section-heading fallback / errored sentinel / unparseable confidence / unparseable SHA / clean-summary negation false-positive guard), gate evaluation (all combinations of failure modes + the PR #652 incident signature), short-SHA prefix matching against full HEAD SHAs, and `main()` exit codes for merge-ready / merge-blocked / no-greptile-comment / gh-failure / `--json` emit. **Atomic-shell-call rule (Mode-1 freshness window):** the swarm SKILL also gains a `!` MUST rule mandating that `task pr:merge-ready -- <N>` and `gh pr merge <N>` run in the same shell call (e.g. `task pr:merge-ready -- <N> && gh pr merge <N> --squash --delete-branch --admin`) so no time elapses between verdict and merge -- a readiness check more than ~60s stale risks Mode-1 false positives where an unrelated commit lands on master in the elapsed window, auto-rebase triggers a fresh Greptile pass, and the new pass surfaces a P1 the cached verdict did not see; plus a corresponding `⊗` MUST NOT rule against running the readiness check upstream of `gh pr merge` (e.g. as a batched cascade-prep step then merging later after intervening rebase / sub-agent dispatch / user discussion). **Lessons cross-reference:** new `## Greptile CheckRun SUCCESS != Review Approval (2026-05)` section in `meta/lessons.md` documenting the PR #652 incident as the recurrence record and the symmetric-blind-spot relationship to the existing #526 NEUTRAL-CheckRun lesson; per the Rule Authority [AXIOM] strongest-applicable-layer block in `main.md`, the entry is a short cross-reference (rule body lives in the deterministic gate + SKILL section, not duplicated in prose) -- generalizable pattern: ANY reviewer-posted CheckRun is a completion signal, not an approval signal. **Greptile P2 fix (PR #797 review):** the empty-body guard in `parse_greptile_body` switched from `if not body:` to `if not body or not body.strip():` to handle the production output of `gh api --jq '... // ""'` -- in raw mode jq emits a trailing newline for empty-string fallbacks, and with `--paginate` jq runs per-page, so a no-comment PR with N pages produces `"\n" * N`. The bare guard treated that as truthy and fell through to the SHA / confidence parsers, producing misleading "Could not parse ..." diagnostics instead of the intended "No Greptile rolling-summary comment found" message (the merge was still correctly blocked, but the diagnostic was wrong). New parametrized regression in `tests/cli/test_pr_merge_readiness.py::TestParseGreptileBody::test_whitespace_only_body_returns_not_found` covers single-newline, 2-page, 4-page, spaces, tab, and mixed-whitespace bodies; new `TestMain::test_no_greptile_comment_production_newline_exits_1` covers the CLI-level production path with both positive (intended diagnostic emitted) and negative (misleading diagnostics absent) assertions. 30 total tests now pass (23 prior + 6 whitespace + 1 production-newline).



### Changed



### Fixed

- **fix(scripts/release.py): release pipeline bypasses #747 branch gate via programmatic env-var (#867)** -- the just-shipped #747 detection-bound branch gate (`.githooks/pre-commit` -> `scripts/preflight_branch.py`, plus `.githooks/pre-push`) refused the in-flight v0.24.0 release-cut at Phase 4 Step 9 because the canonical `task release` pipeline commits release artifacts (CHANGELOG.md, ROADMAP.md, pyproject.toml, uv.lock) on master by design and the gate had no carve-out for that path. The e2e rehearsal did not catch this because the rehearsal's tmp clone is a fresh `git clone` with no `core.hooksPath` configured, so `.githooks/pre-commit` never fires inside the rehearsal -- only operator worktrees that have run `task setup` carry the hooks. The release pipeline is the canonical authorised commit-on-master path, so the fix is programmatic use of the SAME documented operator-side env-var bypass (`scripts/policy.py::ENV_BYPASS = "DEFT_ALLOW_DEFAULT_BRANCH_COMMIT"`) -- not a new bypass, just scoped use of the existing approved escape hatch. New module-level `_release_subprocess_env()` helper returns a copy of `os.environ` with `DEFT_ALLOW_DEFAULT_BRANCH_COMMIT="1"` set, suitable for passing as `env=` to `subprocess.run`/`_run_git`. `_run_git` gained an `env: dict[str, str] | None = None` kwarg defaulting to the pre-#867 behaviour (inherit caller env) so read-only invocations (`git status --porcelain`, `git tag -l`, `git ls-remote`, `git diff --cached`) keep working unchanged. Three call sites in `commit_release_artifacts` (Step 9 -- `git commit`), `create_tag` (Step 10 -- `git tag -a`, defence-in-depth in case a future tag-side hook lands), and `push_release` (Step 11 -- `git push --atomic origin <branch> <tag>`) now call `_release_subprocess_env()` and pass the result as `env=`; each call site carries a one-line `# #867:` comment explaining the bypass. The parent-process `os.environ` is intentionally NEVER mutated -- the env-var lives only in the subprocess env so a stale value cannot leak into a subsequent operator shell session. `scripts/preflight_branch.py` is intentionally untouched per the issue acceptance: the gate's behaviour is correct as-is; the release pipeline must adapt to it. New `tests/cli/test_release_branch_gate.py` (12 tests across `TestReleaseSubprocessEnv`, `TestCommitReleaseArtifactsBranchGate`, `TestCreateTagBranchGate`, `TestPushReleaseBranchGate`, `TestAllThreeMutationsCarryBypass`) mocks `subprocess.run` to capture the `env=` kwarg passed to git commit / tag / push during pipeline-helper invocations; asserts the bypass is present in each; asserts `os.environ` is byte-unchanged after each helper returns (no parent-process pollution); and the aggregate test re-discovers the mutation surface so a future refactor that adds a fourth git mutation without the bypass fails immediately. Closes #867; surfaced during the v0.24.0 release-cut session 2026-05-03 and ships in v0.24.0 to unblock the in-flight cut.

- **fix(skills/swarm): prohibit `git checkout` in another agent's worktree during post-merge cleanup (#800)** -- Phase 6 Step 3 (Update Master) of `skills/deft-directive-swarm/SKILL.md` previously described post-merge `git pull origin <base-branch>` without scoping to the merger's own worktree, which let a merging agent in a multi-worktree swarm pattern `cd` into a sibling worktree another agent owned and run `git checkout master --quiet` to perform the pull -- detaching HEAD on the other agent's branch. Recurrence record: PR #797 merge session (2026-05-01) -- Agent A owned `C:\repos\Deft\directive` on a refinement branch; Agent B (the merger) ran `cd C:\repos\Deft\directive; git checkout master --quiet` after merging its own PR. No work was lost (Agent A had pushed) but recovery was retroactive, not preventative; a future agent's working tree being dirty during the same overreach would have been a higher-severity outcome. Phase 6 Step 3 now carries a new `⊗` MUST NOT rule prohibiting `git checkout` (any branch) in a worktree the merger does not own (post-merge state-update MUST be performed via `git fetch origin <base-branch>` from the merger's OWN worktree, OR left to the human operator) plus a companion `!` MUST rule clarifying that the merger MAY remove its own worktree via `git worktree remove <path>` and delete the orphaned local feature branch via `git branch -D <branch>`, but MUST NOT alter any other worktree's HEAD or branch state. The Anti-Patterns block gains a corresponding `⊗` bullet citing the concrete `cd <other-worktree>; git checkout master --quiet` shape that triggered the recurrence. The new rules cross-reference the existing #727 Sub-Agent Role Separation companion rules earlier in Phase 6 -- #727 codifies sub-agent spawn shape; #800 codifies worktree HEAD operations, the same boundary discipline applied to a different surface. New `tests/content/test_swarm_skill.py` (12 parametrized assertions across 3 sections) regex-asserts Phase 6 Step 3 contains the canonical `⊗` rule tokens (U+2297 glyph guard against cp1252 `Γèù` mojibake), the `!` companion rule tokens, and an Anti-Patterns bullet citing PR #797 + #727 cross-reference + #800 self-citation under a `⊗` marker; mirrors the assertion pattern in `tests/content/test_skills.py` section 39 for the existing #727 Sub-Agent Role Separation tokens. Per the Rule Authority [AXIOM] strongest-applicable-layer rule, the rule body lives in the SKILL prose (no `meta/lessons.md` cross-reference in this PR -- other agents in the same Phase 1 cascade are touching that file). Closes #800.

- **fix(skills/review-cycle): re-fetch on cold-start to catch late-arriving bot reviews (#796)** -- closes the dual-source-fetch blind spot in `skills/deft-directive-review-cycle/SKILL.md` Phase 2 Step 1 where the agent's first fetch can land BEFORE the bot reviewer (Greptile) has posted its review on a freshly-opened PR. Previously the Step 1 dual-source contract (`gh pr view --comments` + MCP `get_review_comments` or `gh api` fallback, with `do_not_summarize_output: true`) correctly caught the `Comments Outside Diff` case but did not cover the cold-start path: if the agent fetched at T+30s after PR creation and Greptile lands at T+3-7min, both sources returned zero findings and Step 6 false-positively declared the PR review-clean. The Step 4 polling loop covered any cycle with a push, but the cold-start one-shot review-cycle entry path was uncovered. New `~` SHOULD rule `**Late-arriving bot review re-check:**` mandates a re-fetch after a ~60s delay before evaluating the Step 6 exit condition when the initial dual-source pass returns no bot review on the current HEAD SHA. Companion `⊗` MUST NOT rule against declaring the exit condition met based on a single empty fetch -- re-fetch at least once after a ~60s delay first. Cross-references the user-rule precedent on dual-source fetching + late-arriving bot reviews and `templates/swarm-greptile-poller-prompt.md` (which already handles this case for push-driven cycles in its loop body) so the rule's scope (cold-start one-shot entry path) is discoverable. New `tests/content/test_review_cycle_skill.py` (8 tests) regex-asserts: the `~` SHOULD rule presence + RFC2119 strength tag, canonical phrasing tokens (`re-fetch`, `60s`, `before evaluating`, `re-fetch at least once`), the `⊗` MUST NOT rule presence, the cross-reference to the poller template, and a defence-in-depth no-cp1252-mojibake guard against the `Γèù` corruption form fixed in the same cohort by PR #844. One-line cross-reference appended to `meta/lessons.md` per the Rule Authority [AXIOM] strongest-applicable-layer rule (the rule body lives in the skill, not duplicated in prose). Closes #796.

- **fix(run): run.bat now resolves the `run` Python entry point against `%~dp0` so `..\deft\run.bat <cmd>` works from any CWD on Windows (#791)** -- closes the adoption blocker where the launcher's `python.exe run %*` line at run.bat:25 resolved the bare `run` token against the caller's CWD instead of the directory of run.bat itself. Consumers who installed deft as `./deft/` and followed the documented `..\deft\run upgrade` invocation from their project root therefore saw `python.exe: can't open file 'run'` because Python looked for the script in the project root, not in `./deft/`. The field workaround (`python.exe "<full path>\deft\run" upgrade`) was undiscoverable. Single-line fix replaces `python.exe run %*` with `python.exe "%~dp0run" %*`; `%~dp0` is the canonical Windows idiom for self-relative path resolution (drive+path of the executing batch file with a trailing backslash), so resolution is now anchored at the launcher's directory regardless of the caller's CWD. Existing in-deft-repo invocations continue to work as a special case of the general rule. Surrounding Python version detection (lines 4-22) and Microsoft Store fallback (lines 28-40) preserved verbatim. New `tests/cli/test_run_bat_path.py` (Windows-conditional via `@pytest.mark.skipif(platform.system() != "Windows")`) carries two tests: a subprocess smoke test that runs `run.bat help` from a fresh `tempfile.TemporaryDirectory` and asserts `returncode == 0` (pre-fix this would fail because the empty tmpdir does not contain a `run` script), plus a static guard that reads `run.bat` and asserts the `"%~dp0run"` idiom is present AND the regression-shape `python.exe run %*` invocation is absent. Closes #791.

- **fix(cmd_doctor): require uv on PATH and surface https://docs.astral.sh/uv/ when missing; replace pre-v0.20 expected_dirs with v0.20+ canonical layout (#792)** -- closes the adoption blocker where `deft/run doctor` reported green on a fresh machine without `uv` installed and then every `task <name>` invocation failed with the opaque `uv: command not found` (every deft task script runs via `uv run python ...`). Two coordinated changes in `run::cmd_doctor`: (1) new required `check_command("uv", "uv (Astral Python runner)", required=True, install_url="https://docs.astral.sh/uv/")` invocation runs first so the failure is the first thing a fresh-machine user sees, plus a new module-level `_check_uv_available()` helper wrapping `shutil.which("uv")` so #793's `task migrate:preflight` aggregate can reuse the detection seam without duplicating the lookup (the install URL pointer mirrors `skills/deft-directive-setup/SKILL.md` § Environment Preflight); the inner `check_command` helper gained an `install_url=""` keyword arg so the URL pointer threads through both required and optional surfaces consistently. (2) `expected_dirs` rewritten from the pre-v0.20 list (`core, languages, interfaces, tools, swarm, templates, meta`) to the v0.20+ canonical layout (`languages, strategies, skills, templates, tasks, scripts, vbrief`), eliminating the spurious `Missing directory: <name>/` warnings the legacy entries produced on every clean checkout. Internal counters split into `errors` and `warnings` so a missing required tool (uv or git) surfaces as a `System check failed with N error(s)` summary above optional-tool warnings AND forces a non-zero exit code for CI clarity; the all-clean and warnings-only paths return the existing exit shape unchanged. New `tests/cli/test_cmd_doctor.py` (6 tests) covers `_check_uv_available` true/false branches, the uv-present and uv-missing cmd_doctor paths (asserting non-zero exit, install URL pointer, and `System check failed` summary on the uv-missing branch), zero `Missing directory:` lines against the live framework checkout (regression guard for the v0.20+ layout), and a defence-in-depth assertion that no pre-v0.20 directory name (`core`, `interfaces`, `tools`, `swarm`, `meta`) appears in the success-line output. The TUI `DoctorScreen` carries a parallel copy of the same legacy `expected_dirs` list and was intentionally left untouched as out-of-scope per the brief boundary -- a follow-up can lift the same fix into the TUI surface. Closes #792.

- **fix(scripts/release.py): refuse early when target tag exists locally, on origin, or as a published GitHub release (#784)** -- closes the adoption blocker where the legacy 12-step release pipeline only invoked `git tag` at Step 9, after Steps 1-8 had already promoted CHANGELOG to `[<version>]`, regenerated ROADMAP, synced `pyproject.toml` + `uv.lock`, built `dist/deft-<version>.zip`, and made a `chore(release): v<version>` commit locally. A duplicate-tag failure at Step 9 stranded the operator with an unpushed wrong-version commit + orphaned dist artifact + manual `git reset --hard origin/master` recovery (forbidden by AGENTS.md SCM rules without explicit permission). Surfaced 2026-05-01 during the v0.23.0 release attempt where the operator typed `0.22.0` (the prior release from 12 hours earlier); the pipeline ran 8 steps before failing at `fatal: tag 'v0.22.0' already exists`. New `check_tag_available(version, repo, project_root)` helper in `scripts/release.py` is a read-only pre-flight that probes three surfaces in order, short-circuiting on first conflict so the FAIL reason names the conflict source: (1) `git tag -l v<version>` (local tag); (2) `git ls-remote --tags origin refs/tags/v<version>` (remote tag on origin -- catches the case where the operator's fetch hasn't run); (3) `gh release view v<version> --repo <owner>/<repo> --json tagName` (published GitHub release -- catches the case where a tag was created via `gh release create` directly without a corresponding ref under `refs/tags/`). Each FAIL reason includes the actionable hint `choose a different version (operator typo of a prior release is the most likely cause)`. The `gh` CLI not on PATH is intentionally NOT a FAIL: the helper passes with an `UNVERIFIED` caveat in the reason (parallel to `verify_release_draft` (#724) gh-missing path) so the local + remote git surfaces still gate the gate even on gh-less hosts; `FileNotFoundError` / `subprocess.TimeoutExpired` from the gh probe are mapped to the same `UNVERIFIED` carve-out per the issue body's explicit `gh-CLI not-found != release-exists` contract. Wired into Phase 1 pre-flight as the new Step 4 (between vBRIEF lifecycle sync at Step 3 and CI at Step 5), so a duplicate-tag failure halts BEFORE any state mutation -- CHANGELOG promotion, ROADMAP refresh, build, commit. Pipeline-step constant `_TOTAL_STEPS` bumps 12 -> 13 (every subsequent label / dry-run preview shifts by one); existing `tests/cli/test_release.py` / `test_release_summary.py` / `test_release_vbrief_lifecycle.py` pipeline-step assertions renumbered accordingly (mirrors the 11 -> 12 shift from #734). Dry-run reports `[4/13] Pre-flight tag availability... DRYRUN (would verify v<version> tag not present locally / on origin / as GitHub release on <repo>)`; production reports `[4/13] Pre-flight tag availability... OK (...)` on clean state, `FAIL (<reason>)` with operator-actionable recovery on conflict. New `tests/cli/test_release_tag_availability.py` (15 tests across `TestCheckTagAvailableHelper`, `TestPipelineStep4`, `TestTotalStepsConstant`) covers clean state OK; local-only / remote-only / GitHub-release-only conflict each FAIL with the named surface; combinations short-circuit on first surface (local before remote before gh); gh-CLI-not-found != release-exists carve-out (both `_resolve_gh()` returning None AND `subprocess.run` raising `FileNotFoundError` paths); local + ls-remote git failures surfaced verbatim with `git tag -l failed: ...` / `git ls-remote failed: ...` reasons; pipeline Step 4 OK proceeds to Step 5 (CI); Step 4 FAIL returns `EXIT_VIOLATION` and never reaches CI; dry-run NEVER invokes the helper (read-only contract is a label-only preview); `_TOTAL_STEPS == 13` constant. `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` Phase 1 gains a new `!` MUST rule citing this issue and the v0.22.0 -> v0.23.0 incident as recurrence record plus a corresponding `⊗` MUST NOT anti-pattern. Closes #784.

- **fix(scripts/preflight_branch.py): UTF-8 self-reconfigure at hook entry to unblock Windows cp1252 commits (#814)** -- closes the HOT Windows adoption blocker where the #747 detection-bound branch gate (installed by `task setup` as `.githooks/pre-commit` + `.githooks/pre-push`) crashed with `UnicodeEncodeError: 'charmap' codec can't encode character '\u2713'` whenever the user's Python stdout defaulted to `cp1252` (the Windows default with `PYTHONIOENCODING` unset). Crucially: the gate had ALREADY APPROVED the commit before the success-path print failed, so the user saw a Python traceback after a successful check, git aborted the commit, and the workaround (`PYTHONIOENCODING=utf-8 git commit ...`) was undiscoverable. New main()-entry block in `scripts/preflight_branch.py` calls `sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8", errors="replace")` (and stderr) BEFORE any print, guarded by `hasattr(..., "reconfigure")` so the call is a no-op on non-`TextIOWrapper` streams (e.g. when stdout is captured by `PIPE`). `errors='replace'` is the belt-and-suspenders fallback so a rare environment that still cannot render UTF-8 sees a printable replacement char rather than an unhandled traceback. **Audit:** `.githooks/pre-commit` and `.githooks/pre-push` both invoke exactly one script under `scripts/` (`scripts/preflight_branch.py`), so the audit surface is fully covered by the single fix; a defence-in-depth audit test re-discovers the hook-invoked surface from `.githooks/` at test time and asserts every script reference is registered against the contract -- a future hook script that lands without the reconfigure block fails immediately. New `tests/cli/test_hooks_encoding.py` (2 tests) pins the contract: a strict `cp1252` `TextIOWrapper` cannot encode U+2713 (sanity); `preflight_branch.main(["--project-root", str(tmp_path)])` invoked under that fake stdout (with `DEFT_SETUP_INTERVIEW=1`) returns 0 cleanly, `sys.stdout.encoding == "utf-8"` after main() runs, and the U+2713 glyph reaches the underlying buffer as canonical UTF-8 bytes (`b'\xe2\x9c\x93'`). **`task setup` advisory:** new informational warning surfaces when `task setup` detects a Python interpreter whose stdout defaults to a Windows code page (`cp1252` / `cp437` / `charmap`); the probe explicitly unsets `PYTHONUTF8` / `PYTHONIOENCODING` in its subshell so it measures what Python would do under git's hook environment (not the Taskfile root `env: PYTHONUTF8: "1"`). Auto-set of `PYTHONIOENCODING` is intentionally NOT done -- mutating the user's environment would surprise other tooling (out-of-scope per the issue body); the warning points at one-time `System Properties > Environment Variables` or PowerShell-profile-level fixes. New `## Windows cp1252 stdout default breaks non-ASCII prints (2026-05)` entry in `meta/lessons.md` codifies the recurring class as a short cross-reference per the Rule Authority [AXIOM] strongest-applicable-layer rule -- the rule body lives in the script + the contract test, prose is fallback only. The success glyph is intentionally preserved as `\u2713` per the issue's Out-of-Scope (fix the encoding, not the UX). Closes #814.

- **fix(vbrief): replace `Γèù` mojibake with canonical `⊗` in #796 / #800 pending briefs (PR #844 review-cycle)** -- Greptile P1 review on PR #844 surfaced 12 occurrences of the cp1252-corrupted prohibition marker (`Γèù` instead of `⊗`) in the two newly-ingested briefs `vbrief/pending/2026-05-03-796-review-cycle-dual-source-fetch-can-miss-late-arriving-bot-re.vbrief.json` (7) and `vbrief/pending/2026-05-03-800-swarm-skill-prohibit-git-checkout-in-a-worktree-another-agen.vbrief.json` (5). A swarm agent following either brief verbatim would have written `Γèù MUST NOT ...` into the target SKILL.md, failing the content-test assertions the briefs themselves prescribe. Fixed via UTF-8-safe Python rewrite (per the user rule against PowerShell 5.1 inline non-ASCII string ops); ironic prelude to the #814 fix that this same cohort tracks. Re-rendered `vbrief/PROJECT-DEFINITION.vbrief.json` (timestamp-only diff -- the corrupted prose did not propagate to the items registry). Refs #796, refs #800.

- **fix(skills,scripts): structural preflight gate prevents unauthorized implementation-agent spawn (#810)** -- closes the implementation-intent-inference adoption blocker where agents reading AGENTS.md inferred implementation intent from lifecycle / branching / PR-process language and spawned code-writing sub-agents without explicit action-verb authorization (the #801-session reproduction was the surfacing event). New `scripts/preflight_implementation.py` is a structural fail-closed gate: takes `--vbrief-path <path>`, exits 0 only when the vBRIEF lives in `vbrief/active/` AND `plan.status == "running"`, exits 1 with the actionable `task vbrief:activate <path>` redirect on every other state (pre-activation folder, wrong status, malformed JSON, missing keys, unreadable file). Pure stdlib, mirrors the `scripts/preflight_branch.py` (#747) shape: `evaluate(path) -> (code, msg)` separated from CLI plumbing for testability, `--json` variant for machine consumers. New `scripts/vbrief_activate.py` is the lifecycle move that satisfies the gate: idempotent (already-active -> no-op, exit 0), validates source is in `vbrief/pending/`, flips `plan.status` from `pending`/`approved` to `running`, stamps `vBRIEFInfo.updated` to current ISO 8601 UTC, atomically moves to `vbrief/active/` via `Path.replace`. New `tasks/vbrief.yml::activate` Taskfile target dispatches the helper with `dir: '{{.USER_WORKING_DIR}}'` consistent with the rest of the lifecycle tasks; no `sources:`/`generates:` per `conventions/task-caching.md`. `skills/deft-directive-build/SKILL.md` gains a new `Step 0 -- Implementation Preflight` section near the top with `!` rules pointing at the helper and the activate task plus `⊗` rules against inferring intent from workflow-shape vocabulary or treating affirmative continuation phrases as implementation authorization; matching anti-pattern entry added. `skills/deft-directive-swarm/SKILL.md` Phase 0 Step 1 deduplicates its inline `active/`-only check by delegating to the helper, surfaces preflight rejections in the Phase 0 Step 4 analysis, and adds a `⊗` rule against spawning agents that haven't passed the gate. New `tests/cli/test_preflight_implementation.py` (24 tests) covers the (folder, status) matrix across `proposed`/`pending`/`active`/`completed`/`cancelled`, edge cases (nonexistent path, directory path, malformed JSON, top-level not-an-object, missing plan, missing/non-string `plan.status`), `--json` schema (stable keys: `ready`/`exit_code`/`vbrief_path`/`message`), main() exit codes + stderr redirect on reject, and the recursively-appropriate self-test asserting the #810 vBRIEF in `vbrief/pending/` is itself rejected by the gate it introduces. New `tests/cli/test_vbrief_activate.py` (15 tests) covers happy path / idempotent no-op / atomic-move durability / collision detection / malformed input. New `tests/content/test_skills_preflight_call.py` regex-asserts both the build and swarm skills carry the `!` MUST line referencing `scripts/preflight_implementation.py` AND the `task vbrief:activate` redirect; failure messages cite file + missing pattern.

- **fix(templates,agents): Implementation Intent Gate documented in AGENTS.md managed-section, propagated by cmd_agents_refresh (#810)** -- prompt-side guardrail companion to the structural fix. New `## Development Process` / `### Implementation Intent Gate (#810)` block lands inside the existing `<!-- deft:managed-section v1 -->` ... `<!-- /deft:managed-section -->` markers in `templates/agents-entry.md` so `cmd_agents_refresh` (#768) propagates it to consumer projects on next refresh; managed-section markers preserved byte-stably (the existing `tests/content/test_agents_entry_contract.py` `test_render_is_byte_stable` assertion continues to pass). Same four-bullet block mirrored in repo-level `AGENTS.md` so the framework dogfoods its own template. The four bullets cover: (a) `!` MUST run `scripts/preflight_implementation.py` before any code-writing tool call; (b) `!` MUST require explicit action-verb directive (`build`/`implement`/`ship`/`swarm`/`run agents`/`start agent`) before invoking the gate; (c) `⊗` MUST NOT infer implementation intent from lifecycle/branching/PR-process language; (d) `⊗` MUST NOT treat affirmative continuation phrases (`yes`/`go`/`proceed`/`do it`) as implementation authorization unless the prior turn explicitly proposed implementation. New tests in `tests/content/test_agents_entry_contract.py` (3 tests) assert the managed-section contains the `Implementation Intent Gate` anchor, the gate region carries at least 4 bullets, and the prefix-token mix is at least 2 `!` AND at least 2 `⊗`; structure/tokens are pinned, not exact wording, so future copy-edits don't break the contract. New `## Implementation-intent inference is a documented anti-pattern (#810)` entry in `meta/lessons.md` codifies the failure mode (trigger phrases like "do the full PR process", "poller agents not local loops" parsed as implementation authorization), the structural gate as the mitigation, and the takeaway that workflow-shape vocabulary is NOT authorization. Closes #810.



### Removed



## [0.23.0] - 2026-05-01



> Phase 1 adoption-blocker batch: branch-policy + branch-gate + universal upgrade gate + framework deterministic-mode rule + interview UX + cost transparency + release-core.



### Added

- **feat(skills,build,cost): pre-build cost & budget transparency phase (#739, refs #151 umbrella)** -- closes the adoption-blocker surfaced by issue #151 (issues #7 and #14 -- the only critical hard blocker in the playtest) where users completed install -> bootstrap -> interview -> PRD -> SPECIFICATION approval and stopped at build because deft offered no cost signal. Three coordinated artifacts plus a build-skill gate plus an AGENTS.md routing entry: (1) **NEW `skills/deft-directive-cost/SKILL.md`** -- dedicated skill (separation of concerns) sitting between SPECIFICATION approval and build kickoff. Plain-English voice for non-technical users (no spreadsheets, no scientific notation, no industry jargon -- explicit ⊗ MUST-NOT rules against `TCO` / `burn rate` / `p50` / `OPEX vs CAPEX` / `amortised` / `blended rate` / `unit economics` / `FTE` in the artifact body and skill prose). Four phases: read the spec & detect categories; draft the artifact; read it back to the user; decision point. The Phase 4 build-kickoff confirmation menu lists six numbered options with `Discuss` and `Back` as the FINAL two per the #767 framework rule (1. Build, 2. Rescope, 3. No-build, 4. Skip, 5. Discuss, 6. Back). Skill carries the canonical RFC2119 legend, a Platform Detection block (Windows `%APPDATA%\deft\USER.md` / Unix `~/.config/deft/USER.md` / `$DEFT_USER_PATH` override) mirroring `skills/deft-directive-build/SKILL.md`, an Inputs block, an Output Targets block, an Anti-Patterns block, and an `## EXIT` block per the AGENTS.md Skill Completion Gate. Plus a `.agents/skills/deft-directive-cost/SKILL.md` thin pointer matching the existing per-skill pattern. (2) **NEW `templates/COST-ESTIMATE.md`** -- canonical body for the per-project artifact produced by the skill: TL;DR, pre-flight account/sign-up summary, hosting/infrastructure rows, API/third-party fee rows, monthly **low / typical / high** band rolled up from the rows above, scale considerations callout when the high band is much bigger than the typical band, build & maintenance time, and an explicit four-way **Decision recorded** block (build / rescope / no-build / skip(+reason)). USD-only first pass; vendor pricing snapshots cited as snapshots, never guarantees; loose ranges only (no single-point estimates). (3) **NEW `references/cost-models.md`** -- captures the cost-model methodology (loose ranges, no hard numbers, USD-only first pass; documented as such). Audience is dual: agents producing the estimate AND non-technical end users reading the artifact. Out-of-scope explicitly enumerated (hard cost numbers tied to 2026 vendor pricing; real-time pricing API integration; currency/region localisation; FinOps for already-running projects). (4) **`skills/deft-directive-build/SKILL.md` Cost Phase Gate (#739)** -- new gate added between the USER.md Gate and File Reading. Refuses kickoff until `COST-ESTIMATE.md` exists AND the **Decision recorded** block carries one of build / rescope / no-build / skip, AND the **Reason** field is populated for skip / rescope / no-build (a skip with no reason is treated the same as no decision). On `build` or `skip`, continues to File Reading; on `rescope`, redirects back to spec edits then re-runs the cost skill; on `no-build`, exits without proceeding to File Reading. Anti-pattern entry added against proceeding without `COST-ESTIMATE.md` and a recorded decision. (5) **`AGENTS.md` Skill Routing entry** -- added a routing line mapping `cost`, `budget`, `pre-build cost`, and `how much will this cost` to `skills/deft-directive-cost/SKILL.md` (only the routing-table section was edited; AGENTS.md Branching / Development Process / PR conventions / session-start disclosure are owned by Agent 1 and were not touched). (6) **Tests** -- new `tests/content/test_cost_phase.py` (34 tests across 7 sections) covers artifact creation (cost skill / template / methodology files exist at expected paths), build-gate behavior (cost-phase gate section present, refuses without `COST-ESTIMATE.md`, decision-state coverage for all four states, skip-requires-reason rule, anti-pattern entry), rescope loop (rescope option present, redirects back to spec edits, re-runs the cost phase), the #767 framework rule (Discuss + Back as the final two consecutive numbered options; Back is the highest-numbered option), template structure (required sections, low/typical/high bands, all four decision options, USD declaration, no jargon in the user artifact), methodology coverage (cost-models.md sections, USD-only documented, loose-ranges promise), and plain-English voice (parametrized check that the listed jargon terms are absent from user-facing skill prose outside the Anti-Patterns and Audience & Voice blocks where they are listed as forbidden). `task check` matches pre-change baseline (3134 passed, 1 xfailed; the 4 broken-link warnings from `task verify:links` are pre-existing -- CHANGELOG.md examples + `scm/changelog.md` template + `templates/swarm-greptile-poller-prompt.md` -- and not introduced by this PR). Closes #739; refs #151 umbrella.

- **feat(framework,skills,policy,scripts,hooks): branch-gate + policy + framework-rule cluster (#564, #746, #747, #767)** -- four cohesive scope changes landed in one branch (`agent1/feat/564-746-747-767-framework-policy-branch-gate`) targeting Phase 1 (`phase-1`).

  - **#746 (no-feature-branch opt-out)** -- promotes the legacy free-form narrative key `Allow direct commits to master:` to a typed boolean `plan.policy.allowDirectCommitsToMaster` on `vbrief/PROJECT-DEFINITION.vbrief.json`. New `Policy` `$def` in `vbrief/schemas/vbrief-core.schema.json` (typed `boolean`; `additionalProperties: true` so future flags can land additively). New `scripts/policy.py` is the single read/write surface (resolution order: env-var bypass `DEFT_ALLOW_DEFAULT_BRANCH_COMMIT`, typed flag, legacy narrative with deprecation warning, default fail-closed). `scripts/policy_set.py` backs `task policy:enforce-branches` and `task policy:allow-direct-commits -- --confirm` (capability-cost disclosure verbatim before the typed flag is written; one-shot legacy-narrative migration in the same write; audit trail to `meta/policy-changes.log`). New `tasks/policy.yml` (no `sources:`/`generates:` per `conventions/task-caching.md`). `skills/deft-directive-setup/SKILL.md` Phase 2 Step 9 elicits the typed flag with the verbatim disclosure + re-prompt; default `false`; existing-flag detection on re-runs surfaces the current value before overwriting; `/deft:policy:*` slash-command alternatives documented. Skill-level guards added at the entry of `deft-directive-{swarm,review-cycle,pre-pr,release}/SKILL.md` halting before any state mutation when the policy is unresolvable AND no env-var bypass is active. Bootstrap fallback: missing PROJECT-DEFINITION fail-closed with helpful error, `--allow-missing-project-definition` flag for the setup-interview hook (#746 acceptance criterion E). AGENTS.md gains a session-start disclosure block when the typed flag is `true`. main.md (mid-file) and README.md (new `## Branch policy` section) cite the policy + enforcement surfaces. Glossary entries: `Branch-protection policy` and `Policy audit log`. **NOTE:** `templates/agents-entry.md` is owned by #768 (Agent 6); the policy-disclosure copy was supplied via `send_message_to_agent` to the parent monitor for incorporation into Agent 6's managed-section content.

  - **#747 (detection-bound branch gate)** -- new `scripts/preflight_branch.py` (Python stdlib-only, cross-platform; reads via `scripts/policy.py`; legacy-narrative fallback with deprecation warning; three-state exit codes: 0 allowed / 1 blocked / 2 config-error; documented `--allow-missing-project-definition` setup-interview exemption hook; `DEFT_SETUP_INTERVIEW=1` exemption; `DEFT_ALLOW_DEFAULT_BRANCH_COMMIT=1` env-var bypass). New `.githooks/pre-commit` and `.githooks/pre-push` POSIX-sh wrappers shelling out to the script (`DEFT_PYTHON` override; falls back to `python3` / `python` discovery). New top-level `task setup` task sets `git config core.hooksPath .githooks` idempotently. New `task verify:branch` wired into the `task check` aggregate (`Taskfile.yml`). New `task verify:hooks-installed` asserts `core.hooksPath==.githooks` and prints the actionable `hooks not installed; run task setup` message on mismatch. New `.github/workflows/branch-gate.yml` GH Actions sanity check refusing PRs whose `head_ref == base_ref` on `pull_request: opened/synchronize/reopened/edited` events. AGENTS.md Branching section gains the `!` cross-reference to all three enforcement surfaces (hooks, verify:branch, branch-gate). README.md `## Branch policy` paragraph + glossary entry coordinated with #746.

  - **#564 (review-cycle stall detection rubric)** -- new `## Stall Detection Rubric (#564)` subsection under Step 4 of `skills/deft-directive-review-cycle/SKILL.md`. Tracks `startedAt` and `commit.oid` per poll; escalates to the user when IN_PROGRESS exceeds 3x expected (~10 minutes for Greptile). User-decision options rendered as a deterministic numbered menu (Wait N min / Manual `@greptileai` re-trigger / Skip with documented reason / Cancel / Discuss / Back). Auto-restart detection resets the elapsed-time clock on a fresh `startedAt` AND notifies the user (silent reset forbidden). Auto-retrigger without explicit user approval forbidden -- the `@greptileai` option requires user pick AND the override MUST be documented in a brief PR comment for auditability. New `## Greptile Review Stall Detection (2026-04)` entry in `meta/lessons.md` capturing the rc4 21-min stall observation on PR #561 as the recurrence record (Stalls past 3x expected MUST escalate, not auto-retrigger; `startedAt` resets MUST notify the user, not silently re-anchor the clock).

  - **#767 (Discuss + Back canonical numbered options)** -- new `contracts/deterministic-questions.md` codifies the rule once: every structured `ask_user_question` prompt (single-select / multi-select) and every numbered-menu prompt rendered in skill prose MUST include `Discuss` and `Back` as the final two numbered options, in that order. The Discuss-pause semantic is documented verbatim (pause IMMEDIATELY, halt the in-progress sequence, no further tool calls beyond acknowledgment, prompt `What would you like to discuss?`, resume only on explicit user signal -- re-asks the original question, says `resume`/`continue`, or re-issues the prior selection; implicit resumption forbidden). The contract includes a `## Prior art reviewed (#431)` section summarising what existed pre-#767 (back-nav, confirm step, escape-hatch distinct from Other) vs what changed (Discuss promoted to peer of Back; no separate Other introduced). `!` cross-references added to `skills/deft-directive-{swarm,setup,refinement,pre-pr,review-cycle,release}/SKILL.md`. NOTE: `skills/deft-directive-interview/SKILL.md` (Agent 2) and `skills/deft-directive-build/SKILL.md` (Agent 3) are explicitly out of scope for this PR -- those agents will land their cross-references in their own PRs. Glossary entry for `Deterministic mode` cross-references the contract. main.md mid-file edit cross-references the contract from the `Decision Making` section. New `tests/content/test_deterministic_questions.py` scans the contract + skill prose and asserts the canonical phrasing, the prior-art section, the cross-references, and the glossary entries.

  - **Tests:** `tests/cli/test_policy.py` (resolution order: typed / legacy narrative / env-var bypass / fail-closed; `set_policy` legacy migration; audit-log creation; `disclosure_line` phrasing; `main` exit codes); `tests/cli/test_policy_set.py` (`enforce-branches` / `allow-direct-commits` with `--confirm` gate; missing PROJECT-DEFINITION returns config-error with recovery pointer); `tests/cli/test_preflight_branch.py` (feature branch / detached HEAD / opted-out / env-var bypass / setup-interview exemption / on-master-blocks / `master` and `main` branch parity / custom default-branch list / legacy narrative with deprecation warning); `tests/content/test_branch_gate.py` (hook scripts exist, Taskfile aggregate `check` includes `verify:branch`, `tasks/verify.yml` declares `branch` + `hooks-installed`, `tasks/policy.yml` declares the three subcommands, the GH Actions workflow rejects `head_ref == base_ref`, AGENTS.md / main.md / README.md / glossary.md / schema all reference the surfaces consistently); `tests/content/test_deterministic_questions.py` (contract verbatim phrasing, prior-art section, skill cross-references, Stall Rubric in review-cycle, lessons.md entry).

- **feat(skills,interview): IP/legal risk flagging during research/interview phase (#738, refs #151 playtest umbrella)** -- new permissive heuristic surfaces third-party intellectual-property (IP) risk before SPECIFICATION generation. New `scripts/ip_risk.py` exposes `detect_ip_terms(text)` (case-insensitive, word-boundary-scoped scan across six categories: branded games/universes, branded characters, sports leagues, branded products, music/film, fictional-universe terms), `is_ip_adjacent(text)`, `ip_risk_scope_items(monetization_intent)` (returns three vBRIEF v0.6 PlanItem-shaped dicts: `IP-1` disclaimer stub, `IP-2` API-only-asset-access policy, `IP-3` hosting policy gated on intent; `Acceptance` narrative tightens for commercial intent to require lawyer-confirmed terms / written license / counsel-reviewed hosting), and `plain_risk_summary(hits, monetization_intent)` (plain-English non-legalese summary that opens with `not legal advice`, names detected categories, and -- for commercial intent -- states explicitly that lawyer consultation is **not optional output** from this interview). New `references/ip-risk.md` codifies the heuristic categories, the canonical monetization-intent question script (Personal vs Commercial vs Other; defaulting to Commercial because the stricter checklist is the wrong-side-of-safe choice), and the minimum-protection checklist with per-intent acceptance criteria. New IP Risk Probe section in `skills/deft-directive-interview/SKILL.md` MUST run the heuristic when capturing the project description, ask the monetization-intent question on detection, emit the plain-English summary into the interview output AND an `IPRisk` narrative on the spec vBRIEF, inject the three protection scope items into `plan.items` (flowing naturally into the rendered SPECIFICATION.md via the existing `scripts/spec_render.py` pipeline -- no spec_render.py modification required), and surface the non-optional lawyer-consultation recommendation for commercial intent before the confirmation gate. New `IPRisk` narrative section in `strategies/research.md` carries the same probe at the research phase. Tests: 26 unit tests in `tests/scripts/test_ip_risk.py` (positive + negative detection across all six categories, case-insensitive matching, word-boundary scoping that rejects substring matches in unrelated words like `magicwand`/`starcraft`, dedupe of repeated terms, commercial-vs-personal-vs-unknown branching for scope items + summary, scope-item shape conformance to vBRIEF v0.6 PlanItem with traces `IP-1`/`IP-2`/`IP-3`, plain-English summary content + legalese-token rejection, CLI three-state exit codes); 18 content tests in `tests/content/test_ip_risk_skill.py` (interview skill IP Risk Probe section presence + helper references + minimum-protection checklist names + lawyer-non-optional rule; research strategy IPRisk narrative; reference doc heuristic / question-script / minimum-protection / canonical-helper sections + legal-advice disclaimer). Closes #738.

- **feat(run,templates,docs): universal upgrade gate + AGENTS.md contract + cmd_agents_refresh** (#768): Closes the stale-AGENTS.md adoption-blocker surfaced by the Timmy session reproduction (v0.5-installed consumer with `deft/` bumped to v0.22 silently followed pre-v0.20 phase logic via the read-AGENTS.md-and-follow-it path; existing gates only fired on CLI invocation (#410), sync-skill trigger phrases, or paths the agent did not take). Five coordinated changes share one principle -- the gate is upgrade-path-agnostic, the framework owns the AGENTS.md contract, UPGRADING.md is the only source of truth per state. (1) New `cmd_gate` in `run` -- read-only state-vector probe emitting `OK v<current>` or `NEEDS-UPGRADE recorded=<recorded|unknown> current=<current> precutover=<csv|empty> agents-md=<current|stale|missing|absent>` with `--json` variant; reuses `_read_version_marker`, `_detect_pre_cutover_legacy`, `_running_inside_deft_repo`, dynamic `VERSION` (#741); no marker writes, no migrations, no commits; the `agents-md=` axis is computed via `_classify_agents_md` against the rendered template. (2) New `cmd_agents_refresh` in `run` -- Python reference implementation of the AGENTS.md contract; `--dry-run` shows the planned change, `--check` exits 0 only when the consumer's managed section is byte-identical to the rendered template; reads `templates/agents-entry.md`, handles four states (`current` / `stale` / `missing` / `absent`); legacy-to-marker migration on first run preserves consumer notes above the bracketed region. `cmd_upgrade` now calls `cmd_agents_refresh` automatically alongside writing `vbrief/.deft-version`. (3) Universal `<!-- DEFT-PREAMBLE-V1 -->` preamble injected at line 1 of `main.md` plus every legacy redirect stub enumerated by the `git --no-pager log --all -- cmd/deft-install/setup.go` audit (`skills/deft-setup/SKILL.md`, `skills/deft-build/SKILL.md`, root `SKILL.md`); the preamble instructs the agent to run `python3 deft/run gate` before any other instruction in the file and on non-zero exit to read `deft/UPGRADING.md` and follow the section whose `Applies when` clause matches the printed state vector, honoring any `Restart required` directive. (4) Contract artifacts: `<!-- deft:managed-section v1 --> ... <!-- /deft:managed-section -->` markers added to `templates/agents-entry.md` (versioned for future format detection); new `templates/agents-entry.placeholders.md` documents the placeholder spec (`UPSTREAM_SHA`, `UPSTREAM_REF`, `UPSTREAM_TAG`, `FETCHED_AT`, `FETCHED_BY` -- inherited from the webinstaller pin-marker contract); rail-agnostic conformance test `tests/content/test_agents_entry_contract.py` asserts the template parses, placeholders match the spec, markers are well-formed, and byte-identical refresh produces byte-identical output. (5) UPGRADING.md retrofit: every `## From <prev> -> <new>` section now carries the four-field micro-format header (`Applies when` / `Safe to auto-run` / `Restart required` / `Commands`); `tests/content/test_upgrading_sections.py` enforces the contract going forward. New CLI tests `tests/cli/test_cmd_gate.py` cover all four `agents-md=` states + version drift + pre-cutover combinations + `--json` structure; `tests/cli/test_cmd_agents_refresh.py` covers fresh write / marker round-trip / legacy-to-marker migration / `--check` exit codes / `--dry-run` output / idempotency. `tests/content/test_main_md_preamble.py` asserts the preamble marker is present at line 1 of every required file. Manual repro evidence: a v0.5-state fixture bumped to current; agent reads `./AGENTS.md`; runs gate; gets `NEEDS-UPGRADE recorded=0.5.0 current=<current> precutover= agents-md=missing`; reads `UPGRADING.md`; executes the matching section's commands (including `deft/run agents:refresh` via `deft/run upgrade`); halts with the start-fresh-session message. Closes #768.

- **feat(release,scripts): keep pyproject version truthful + PEP 440 normalization helper** (#771, refs #74 release pipeline parent, refs #723 CLI/Taskfile resolver, refs #716 release safety hardening, refs #11 future pip packaging extension hook): Closes the v0.21.0-era drift bug where `pyproject.toml` `[project].version` reported `0.5.0` long after `v0.22.0` had shipped. Two coordinated phases plus a documented Phase C hook for future pip packaging. **Phase A (stop lying now):** `scripts/release.py` Step 5 now syncs `[project].version` in `pyproject.toml` from the resolved release version on every real release -- new pure helper `update_pyproject_version(text, version)` rewrites only the FIRST `version = "..."` line under the `[project]` section (sub-tables like `[tool.poetry]` are intentionally untouched), idempotent on re-run; new `_sync_pyproject_for_release(path, version, *, dry_run)` outcome wrapper surfaces the operator-readable status inline (`pyproject [project].version -> X.Y.Z` / `pyproject already at X.Y.Z` / `non-publishable tag ...; skipping pyproject sync` / `no pyproject.toml; skipping sync`) and threads through the existing Step 5 OK / DRYRUN / FAIL labels without bumping `_TOTAL_STEPS`; `pyproject.toml` joins `_RELEASE_ARTIFACTS` so the commit step stages it alongside CHANGELOG.md / ROADMAP.md and the annotated tag anchors at the synced commit. Root `pyproject.toml` `[project].version` updated 0.5.0 -> 0.22.0 to match the latest tag, with an inline comment citing #771 + the freshness test. New regression gate `tests/content/test_pyproject_version_freshness.py` (3 tests) fails if pyproject drifts from `to_pep440(latest tag)`, with explicit skip paths for non-publishable tags (`v0.0.0-test.N`) and missing-git scenarios. **Phase B (PEP 440 normalization):** new canonical helper `scripts/resolve_version.py::to_pep440(version)` -- the SINGLE normalization rule across release-tag / CLI / PyPI surfaces, mapping `v0.22.0` -> `0.22.0`, `v0.20.0-rc.3` -> `0.20.0rc3`, `v0.20.0-beta.2` -> `0.20.0b2`, `v0.20.0-alpha.1` -> `0.20.0a1`, and explicitly classifying disposable `v0.0.0-test.N` tags as non-publishable via a new `NonPublishableVersionError` exception (subclasses `ValueError` for backward-compatible catch blocks); companion `is_publishable(version)` returns False for both non-publishable and malformed inputs. The release pipeline catches `NonPublishableVersionError` in Step 5 and skips the pyproject sync rather than failing -- disposable rehearsal tags from `task release:e2e` (#716) never propagate into PyPI / consumer-visible metadata. **Phase C hook:** `scripts/resolve_version.py` module docstring + `TestPep440PhaseCExtensionHook` regression test document the contract that any future pip-packaging path (root-repo distribution, dedicated wrapper package per #11) MUST consume `to_pep440` rather than reimplementing the rule -- exactly one normalization rule across all version surfaces. **Docs:** new `docs/versioning.md` documents the three canonical version sources (CLI/runtime, release-tag, Python-package), the authority matrix (tag is the single source of truth; pyproject is a derived artifact), the non-publishable tag handling, and the Phase C extension contract. **Tests:** 22 new `to_pep440` cases in `tests/cli/test_resolve_version.py` (stable / rc / alpha / beta mappings + non-publishable + malformed + `is_publishable` + canonical acceptance table); 17 new tests in `tests/cli/test_release_pyproject_sync.py` covering the pure helper + outcome helper + pipeline Step 5 integration + `_RELEASE_ARTIFACTS` constant guard + commit-step staging; the freshness regression test at `tests/content/test_pyproject_version_freshness.py`. Note: GitHub label on #771 says "Phase 4" but absorbed into Phase 1 swarm per 2026-04-30 swarm planning. Closes #771.

### Changed

- **feat(skills,interview): plain-English UX pass -- jargon, approval menus, diff preface (#740, refs #151 playtest umbrella, refs #767 deterministic-questions framework rule)** -- closes the consumer-adoption defect cluster surfaced by the #151 playtest where non-technical users only completed the planning flow because they had a second AI translating jargon, decoding ambiguous approval actions, and explaining red/green diffs. Three coordinated UX rules across `skills/deft-directive-interview/SKILL.md` and `strategies/interview.md`: (1) **Jargon pass** -- every technical question MUST carry a one-line plain-English context note as preamble above the structured-tool call (per Rule 2 Preamble Placement), every acronym MUST be defined inline on first use (`PRD (Product Requirements Document)`, `NFR`, `FR`, `SPEC`, `API`, `DB`, `CI`, `MVP`), and every framework recommendation MUST either explain the rationale in plain-English terms the user actually cares about (cost, speed, hiring, hosting compatibility) OR remove the rationale entirely and present it as an overridable default -- one-word `industry-standard` / `modern` / `scalable` justifications are a ⊗ anti-pattern. (2) **Approval-menu pass** -- explicit numbered approval menu after PRD review AND after SPEC review with action-shaped labels (`1. Approve and continue` / `2. Suggest changes` / `3. Edit yourself` / `4. Discuss` / `5. Back`). The menus follow the **#767 deterministic-questions framework rule**: the final two numbered options MUST be `Discuss` and `Back`, in that order. The framework rule itself is being landed by Agent 1 in #767; this PR cross-references it with a `!` MUST cross-reference at every menu site so once `contracts/deterministic-questions.md` exists this surface defers to it for canonical wording. (3) **Diff-view preface pass** -- when a PRD or SPECIFICATION review surfaces a red/green diff, the agent MUST emit a one-line non-alarming preface above it (`Here's what changed since the previous draft. Red lines were removed, green lines were added. Nothing here is broken -- this is a normal review.`) OR hide the diff entirely on the first review pass and present a plain-English summary instead. New `references/plain-english-ux.md` codifies all six rules (plain-English context note, acronyms-on-first-use, framework justifications explained-or-removed, numbered approval menu with Discuss/Back final-two per #767, diff-view preface, audience test) plus canonical PRD-review and SPECIFICATION-review approval menus and an Anti-Patterns block. Tests: 30 content tests in `tests/content/test_plain_english_ux.py` covering reference-doc rule presence, acronym-on-first-use rule named in interview surfaces, approval-menu presence (PRD + SPEC), diff-preface presence (skill + strategy PRD section + strategy SPEC section), Discuss/Back-final-two assertion via regex extractor that walks numbered-menu blocks and checks `menu[-2]` contains `Discuss` and `menu[-1]` contains `Back` on every approval menu in interview SKILL + interview strategy + reference doc canonical menus, and #767 cross-reference assertions. Closes #740.

- **chore(vbrief): consistent `PhaseDescription` on every Phase 2 brief** -- set the same canonical text ("Near-up structural priority -- post-cutover stabilization, structural unblockers (items gating many others), and cross-cutting items whose effect spans multiple skills, strategies, or files.") on every Phase 2 brief in `pending/` (#481, #624, #627, #628, #629, #630, #762, plus the three #635 children promoted this session). Defends against the renderer's first-wins behaviour where different `PhaseDescription` values across same-phase briefs would silently surface whichever one sorts first by filename. The medium-term structural fix (centralise in PROJECT-DEFINITION) is tracked at #762.

- **chore(vbrief): scope narrowing on #622** -- after analysis, scope split: Improvement 2 (communication bridge filter for the coding agent) stays in `deft-directive-review-cycle`; Improvement 1 (clean-context reviewer principle) routed to `deftai/slizard#124` because the constraint is a property of the reviewer system, not something a downstream consumer can enforce. Brief title narrowed accordingly; references updated to canonical v0.6 shape (`{uri, type: x-vbrief/github-issue, title}`) and cross-link the slizard companion. Scope-split note posted on #622.

- **chore(vbrief): reference shape normalised on auto-ingested briefs** -- the briefs ingested via `task issue:ingest` for #622, #623, and #627 carried the legacy `{type, id, url}` reference shape; promotions normalised to the canonical v0.6 `{uri, type: x-vbrief/github-issue, title}` shape used by every other lifecycle brief. Same shape used in the new pending briefs filed this session (#759, #760, #761, #762).

- **chore(vbrief): metadata cleanup on briefs that stay in `proposed/`** -- two briefs intentionally remain in `proposed/` after this pass: #625 (blocked by #481 which was promoted this session) and the #635 phase-0-spec-scaffolding-rfc (self-gated on its own discussion phase). Both got blocker-status updates reflecting PR #401 cleared. The Phase 0 RFC additionally gained an `x-migrator.Phase: "Phase 2"` + canonical `PhaseDescription` so future promotion lands at the correct phase without the operator needing to remember; an `Urgency` narrative key flags that running the discussion is near-term priority because it gates half of #233's tail. The #212 discussion-only brief stays in `proposed/` per its existing classification (DO NOT IMPLEMENT until team decision reached).



### Fixed

- **fix(scripts): script-bug cluster -- `spec_validate` v0.6 envelope message + wired `VALID_VBRIEF_VERSIONS`, `apply_lifecycle_fixes` dedup, PRD `--force` recovery audit (#565, #573, #756)**: Three coordinated script-level fixes lifted from the 2026-04-30 Phase 1 refinement cohort, batched into a single PR per the orchestrator role-separation guidance (#727).

  - **(#565) `scripts/spec_validate.py`** -- the legacy-flat-format error string near line 177 still pointed operators at "Migrate to vBRIEF v0.5 envelope" after the v0.6 strict tightening (#533) retired the v0.5 envelope; corrected to "Migrate to vBRIEF v0.6 envelope". Concurrently wired the `VALID_VBRIEF_VERSIONS: frozenset[str] = frozenset({"0.6"})` constant into the `vBRIEFInfo.version` check (Option B from the issue) so this validator now matches `scripts/vbrief_validate.py`'s pattern; a future v0.7 introduction adds one entry to the frozenset rather than touching multiple inline string comparisons. New regression tests in `tests/cli/test_spec.py`: `test_validate_legacy_flat_format_advertises_v06_envelope` (positive `"v0.6 envelope"` + negative `"v0.5 envelope"` assertion guards against silent revert), `test_validate_valid_vbrief_versions_constant` (frozenset shape), and `test_validate_version_check_uses_valid_vbrief_versions` (behavioural guard: a v0.5-envelope vBRIEF is still rejected with the canonical migration hint). Closes #565.

  - **(#573) `scripts/prd_render.py`** -- verified that #574 (drop `sources:` / `generates:` from `tasks/prd.yml`) resolved the original `task prd:render -- --force` no-op repro; the script-level `--force` flag is now the canonical recovery surface for the #539 refuse-to-overwrite check. Added two regression tests in `tests/cli/test_prd_render.py` (`test_prd_render_refuses_to_overwrite_without_force`, `test_prd_render_force_recovery_overwrites_prd`) that follow the #539 message's recovery command literally and assert PRD.md is overwritten with the auto-generated banner. **Audit findings**: the only `tasks/*.yml` entry that retains `sources:` / `generates:` after #574 is `tasks/deployments.yml::cloudgov:export`, which uses `cp` and accepts no script-level `--force`-like flag -- a legitimate build-cache use case, not the #573 shape. `tasks/ci.yml::local`, `tasks/pr.yml::check-protected-issues` / `pr:check-closing-keywords`, and `tasks/migrate.yml::vbrief` all already omit caching with explicit comments citing `conventions/task-caching.md` (#574). No further `tasks/*.yml` cleanup required. Closes #573.

  - **(#756) `scripts/reconcile_issues.py::apply_lifecycle_fixes`** -- pre-compute the unique candidate set of vBRIEF rel paths before the move loop so a vBRIEF referencing N closed issues is processed exactly once. Previously the loop iterated per closed-issue Section (c) entry; the first move succeeded and the next N-1 attempts failed with the spurious `vBRIEF file missing` diagnostic, exiting 1 with `failures != []` even though the lifecycle move was correct. `dict.fromkeys(...)` preserves first-seen order so the `[N/M] vBRIEFs reconciled` summary stays stable across runs; the candidate counter at the call site is updated to dedupe identically. New tests `TestApplyDedupesMultiReferenceVbrief::test_apply_dedupes_multi_reference_vbrief` (synthetic report with one vBRIEF in three Section (c) entries; asserts `moved == 1`, `failures == []`, file lands in `completed/` exactly once) and `test_apply_dedupes_includes_completed_skip_path` (defence-in-depth: a multi-reference vBRIEF already in `completed/` increments `skipped` exactly once after dedup) added to `tests/cli/test_reconcile_issues_apply.py`. Existing happy-path tests in the same module continue to pass unchanged. Closes #756.

- **fix(tasks/core.yml,scripts/build_dist.py): cross-platform `task build` artifact parity (#736)** -- the prior `tasks/core.yml::build` shape dispatched `tar -czf ... --exclude=...` on linux/darwin and `powershell -NoProfile -Command "Compress-Archive -Path . -DestinationPath dist\deft-X.Y.Z.zip -Force"` on windows. The Windows branch had no exclude list so the produced zip ingested `.git/` (often hundreds of MB of history), `backup/`, `node_modules/`, AND -- because `Compress-Archive -Path .` walks the output directory recursively -- the prior `dist/` artifact, leading to unbounded growth on every re-run. CI never caught this because no test asserted shape parity across the platform branches. New `scripts/build_dist.py` (stdlib-only via `tarfile` / `zipfile`) replaces the platform split with a single Python helper that uses one canonical exclude list (`.git`, `dist`, `backup`, `node_modules`, plus the Python-tooling caches `__pycache__`, `.venv`, `htmlcov`, `.pytest_cache`, `.mypy_cache`, `.ruff_cache`, `.coverage`), auto-selects `tar.gz` on Linux/macOS and `zip` on Windows (overridable via `--format`), and accepts an optional `--exclude-extra` flag to extend the canonical set. Idempotent re-run is guaranteed structurally by including `dist` in the canonical exclude list -- a stale prior artifact at `dist/deft-<version>.<ext>` cannot be ingested because the directory is pruned during `os.walk` traversal. `tasks/core.yml::build` now dispatches a single `uv run python {{.DEFT_ROOT}}/scripts/build_dist.py --version {{.VERSION}}` command (no platform split); the same simplification lands on `tasks/core.yml::clean` (replaces the `rm -rf dist/` + `Remove-Item -Recurse -Force dist` duplication with a single `uv run python -c "import shutil, pathlib; ..."` command using `shutil.rmtree`). New `tests/cli/test_build_dist.py` (parametrized over linux-tar / windows-zip / macos-tar) covers excluded-path correctness, expected-core-paths-present (`scripts/`, `skills/`, `tasks/`, `AGENTS.md`), 50 MB sanity ceiling, idempotent re-run (with a marker file added between runs to make regression visible), `--exclude-extra` flag, CLI surface (argparse, three-state exit codes), and an end-to-end smoke test that invokes `task build` against the real repo (skipped when `task` is not on PATH; mirrors the pattern in `tests/content/test_taskfile_caching.py` and `tests/content/test_taskfile_release_names.py`). New `tests/content/test_taskfile_zip_parity.py` parses `tasks/core.yml` and asserts the `build` task uses a single cross-platform command with no `cmds[].platforms` entries, dispatches via `scripts/build_dist.py`, and is collapsed to <=2 cmds; mirror assertions guard the `clean` task's simplification (no `platforms:` split, no `powershell`, no `rm -rf`). Closes #736.

- **fix(scripts/reconcile_issues.py): bump `ISSUE_FETCH_LIMIT` 200 -> 1000** (#764): the deftai/directive repo crossed 200 open issues during the 2026-04-30 refinement cycle, so every `task issue:ingest -- --all [--label X]` run printed `Warning: fetched 200 issues (limit 200). Report may be incomplete.` and silently excluded older issues from dedup/coverage. Single-line constant change couples `ISSUE_FETCH_LIMIT` to the existing `DEFAULT_MAX_OPEN_ISSUES` ceiling already declared in the same file. New regression test `test_issue_fetch_limit_floor` asserts `ISSUE_FETCH_LIMIT >= DEFAULT_MAX_OPEN_ISSUES` so the two safety values cannot drift apart in a future refactor. Existing `test_limit_warning_printed_when_at_cap` is value-agnostic (monkeypatches the constant) and continues to pass. Closes #764.

- **chore(rendered-artifacts): refreshed `ROADMAP.md` + `vbrief/PROJECT-DEFINITION.vbrief.json` after the lifecycle moves** via `task roadmap:render` and `task project:render`. The items registry now reflects 313 scope items across the lifecycle folders post-cleanup; `ROADMAP.md` Phase 2 surfaces all eight Phase 2 briefs in the rendered output with the canonical PhaseDescription.

## [0.22.0] - 2026-04-30



> Release-pipeline trust: lifecycle-gate scaling + draft auto-flip and VERSION drift fixes. Plus pre-PR/CLI gates, README cleanup, and pytest+pygments security bumps.



### Added

- **feat(cli): enforce USER.md gate in `cmd_spec` and `cmd_project` (#163)** -- mirror the agentic-path USER.md gate documented in `skills/deft-directive-build/SKILL.md` ("USER.md Gate" section) at the two CLI entry points that consume user-scoped defaults. Two new helpers in `run`: `_resolve_user_md_path()` resolves USER.md per platform (Windows: `%APPDATA%\deft\USER.md`; Unix: `~/.config/deft/USER.md`) with `$DEFT_USER_PATH` always taking precedence on any platform; `_check_user_md_gate()` returns `1` and emits a `print_error` redirect ("USER.md not found at <path>", "Run 'run bootstrap' to create your user preferences before continuing.", "Set $DEFT_USER_PATH to override the default location.") when USER.md is missing, or `None` to let the caller continue. `cmd_spec` and `cmd_project` invoke the gate before any prompts or work so a missing USER.md exits non-zero with an actionable message instead of silently generating a scope vBRIEF / PROJECT-DEFINITION that lacks the user defaults (languages, coverage, strategy) downstream tooling depends on. The gate intentionally lives at the function entry (not in `main()`'s dispatcher) so `cmd_install` and `cmd_bootstrap`'s post-success chain into `cmd_project` / `cmd_spec` go through the same check. New `tests/cli/test_usermd_gate.py` (9 tests) covers all three plan.items from `vbrief/active/2026-04-23-163-...vbrief.json`: resolver honors `$DEFT_USER_PATH` override; `_check_user_md_gate()` returns `None` when present and `1` when missing (with redirect message asserted via `capsys`); `cmd_spec` and `cmd_project` both block at the gate when USER.md is missing (asserts non-zero exit, no output file written, message names the resolved path AND `run bootstrap`); both commands proceed normally when USER.md is present at the resolved path; both commands honor the `$DEFT_USER_PATH` override against a custom tmp_path location -- bypassing the standard `isolated_env*` fixtures so the developer's real USER.md is never touched. New `tests/cli/conftest.py` overrides the parent `isolated_env` fixture (defined in `tests/conftest.py`) to additionally pre-create a minimal USER.md at `$DEFT_USER_PATH` so existing CLI tests (cmd_spec / cmd_project happy paths in `test_cmd_spec.py`, `test_project.py`, `test_spec_sizing.py`, `test_loop_bugs.py::test_project_*`, `test_project_user_defaults.py`) keep passing without per-test edits; sibling `isolated_env_no_user` fixture exposes the absence path for the new gate tests, the gate-flip in `test_project_user_defaults.py::test_project_blocks_when_user_md_missing` (replaces the prior `test_project_still_works_without_user_md` whose semantics inverted with this change), the `test_read_user_defaults_returns_none_when_missing` unit test, and the `cmd_bootstrap` tests in `test_bootstrap.py` / `test_resume.py` / `test_loop_bugs.py::test_bootstrap_*` (which write USER.md as their primary behavior under test). `task check` green (2983 passed, 1 xfailed). Scope vBRIEF: `vbrief/active/2026-04-23-163-enforce-user-md-gate-in-cli-path-parity-with-agentic.vbrief.json`. Closes #163.

- **feat(scripts,skills): vBRIEF-lifecycle reconciliation gate (#734)** -- new `--apply-lifecycle-fixes` flag on `scripts/reconcile_issues.py` moves Section (c) (closed-issue) vBRIEFs from `proposed/` / `pending/` / `active/` into `completed/`, sets `plan.status = "completed"`, and stamps `vBRIEFInfo.updated`; idempotent on re-run; tolerant of both legacy bare `github-issue` and canonical `x-vbrief/github-issue` reference shapes; reverse mismatches (vBRIEFs in `completed/` whose origin issue reopened) are reported via the existing reconcile output but never auto-reverse-moved (operator decision per the vBRIEF). New `scripts/release.py::check_vbrief_lifecycle_sync(project_root, repo)` helper wraps the same `reconcile_issues` surface and is wired into the release pipeline as a brand-new Step 3 between branch guard (Step 2) and CI (Step 4); the helper returns a three-state result (clean / mismatch-fail / config-error) and the pipeline emits `[3/12] Pre-flight vBRIEF lifecycle sync... OK|FAIL|SKIP|DRYRUN` lines so operators can tail the run. The pipeline-step constant `_TOTAL_STEPS` bumps 11 -> 12 (every subsequent label / dry-run preview shifts by one); existing test_release.py / test_release_summary.py pipeline-step assertions are renumbered accordingly. New `--allow-vbrief-drift` escape-hatch flag (default False; analogous to `--allow-dirty`) lets the operator override after explicit acknowledgment, e.g. for emergency hot-fix releases where the lifecycle reconcile is intentionally deferred to the next refinement pass. The clean recovery path is `task reconcile:issues -- --apply-lifecycle-fixes`. `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` Phase 1 gains a `!` MUST rule citing the v0.21.0 cut as the recurrence record (13 stranded vBRIEFs surfaced post-publish: 8 cycle-relevant + 5 historical residue) plus a corresponding `⊗` MUST NOT anti-pattern. `meta/lessons.md` carries a short cross-reference entry (`## vBRIEF Lifecycle Drift on Release (2026-04)`) per the Rule Authority [AXIOM] strongest-applicable-layer rule -- the rule body lives in the deterministic gate, not in prose. Tests: 14 new tests across `tests/cli/test_reconcile_issues_apply.py` (apply-mode happy path / idempotent re-run / mixed reference shapes / reverse-mismatch / no-issue-ref skip / report-only default / conflict handling) and `tests/cli/test_release_vbrief_lifecycle.py` (`check_vbrief_lifecycle_sync` clean / mismatch / completed-folder excluded / vbrief-dir-missing / gh-failure; pipeline Step 3 wiring; `--allow-vbrief-drift` escape hatch; `_TOTAL_STEPS == 12` constant; argparse round-trip).

- **feat(scripts,tasks,skills): pre-PR closing-keyword negation-context lint (#737)** -- new `scripts/pr_check_closing_keywords.py` scans the PR body AND every commit message in the PR for closing-keyword tokens (`close|closes|closed|fix|fixes|fixed|resolve|resolves|resolved`) followed by `#\d+` in negation, quotation, example, or fenced-code-block contexts. Three-state exit (0 clean / 1 hits found / 2 config error). Pure stdlib + `gh` CLI; supports `--pr <N>` (online via `gh pr view`), `--body-file <path>` / `--commits-file <path>` (offline pre-push hooks / CI), and `--allow-known-false-positives <issue-numbers>` to suppress legitimately-quoted occurrences (test fixtures, documentation that exercises the trigger token). New `tasks/pr.yml` entry `pr:check-closing-keywords` (NO `sources:` / `generates:` per `conventions/task-caching.md`, so user-facing recovery flags are never silently swallowed by go-task's incremental-build cache) wraps the script. `skills/deft-directive-pre-pr/SKILL.md` Phase 4 (Diff) gains a `!` MUST rule invoking the lint pre-push and a `⊗` MUST NOT anti-pattern in the Anti-Patterns block citing the recurrence record (#697 closed #642, #401 closed #642, #700 closed #233, #735 closed #734). `skills/deft-directive-swarm/SKILL.md` Phase 6 Step 1 gains a Layer 0 (prevention) vs Layer 3 (recovery, #701) cross-reference so monitors know to invoke the Layer 0 lint pre-push BEFORE running the Layer 3 `pr:check-protected-issues` pre-merge inspection. `meta/lessons.md` extends the existing `## GitHub Closing-Keyword False-Positive in Negation Context (2026-04)` entry with a third recurrence-record bullet citing #735 and #737 as the structural gap-closer. Tests: 22 new tests across `tests/cli/test_pr_check_closing_keywords.py` (per-context detection: negation / quotation / example / code-block / blockquote / true-positive control; `--pr` mode end-to-end with stubbed `gh`; offline `--body-file` / `--commits-file` modes; `--allow-known-false-positives` escape hatch; three-state exit codes) and `tests/content/test_pre_pr_skill_closing_keyword_rule.py` (Phase 4 rule + recurrence record + anti-pattern; swarm Layer 0 cross-reference present).



### Changed

- **chore(deps): bump pytest 9.0.2 -> 9.0.3 and pygments 2.19.2 -> 2.20.0** (Dependabot alerts #4 and #3): Closes two open security alerts on `uv.lock`. (1) `pytest` GHSA-6w46-j5rx-g56g / CVE-2025-71176 (medium) -- vulnerable tmpdir handling on UNIX where pytest <9.0.3 relies on `/tmp/pytest-of-{user}` directories that allow local users to cause denial of service or possibly gain privileges; bump to 9.0.3 (first patched). (2) `pygments` GHSA-5239-wwwm-4pmq / CVE-2026-4539 (low) -- ReDoS in `AdlLexer` via inefficient regex in `pygments/lexers/archetype.py`; bump to 2.20.0 (first patched). Both are dev-group dependencies (pygments transitive via pytest); `task check` passes (3020 passed, 1 xfailed) post-upgrade.
